                  Introduction and Summary

                  Introduction
                  This report presents the results of a traffic impact analysis for the proposed Delta Products Development
                  in the City of Fremont. The proposed Delta Products Development consists of a 178,327-sq. ft. of
                  Research & Development (R&D) three-story building. The currently vacant parcel of 15.5 acres is located
                  at the southwest corner of Fremont Boulevard/Cushing Parkway intersection.

                  The report includes the results of traffic operations analysis for study intersections, signal warrant analysis
                  and recommendations and site access analysis.

                  Summary
                  TJKM has reached the following conclusions regarding the proposed Delta Products Development in the
                  City of Fremont:

                  The proposed Delta Products Development of 178,327 sq. ft. is expected to generate 1,446 daily trips,
                  including 218 a.m. peak hour trips and 191 p.m. peak hour trips on a typical weekday.

                  Under Existing Conditions, all the study intersections are operating at an acceptable LOS D or better except
                  for the intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection during the p.m. peak hour.

                  Under Background Conditions with the addition of approved / pending project traffic, all the study
                  intersections are expected to continue to operate at an acceptable LOS D or better except for the
                  intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection during the p.m. peak hour.

                  Under Project Conditions, with the addition of project traffic to the Background Conditions, all the study
                  intersections are expected to continue to operate at an acceptable LOS D or better except for the
                  intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection. During the p.m. peak hour, this
                  unsignalized study intersection would operate at LOS F with a minor street average delay of 50.7
                  seconds/vehicle (sec/veh) for site access Alternative 1. Under site access Alternative 2, the Fremont
                  Boulevard/Landing Parkway/project access intersection would operate at LOS F in both the a.m. peak hour
                  and the p.m. peak hour with two-way stop control on the minor streets. It is recommended that the all-
                  way access for the project site be provided at the existing T-intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing
                  Parkway as shown on Figure 3 (Proposed Site Plan-Alternative 2), and that this intersection be signalized
                  and an exclusive left-turn lane be added on the northbound approach to provide acceptable LOS
                  operations.

                  TJKM conducted an ACTC analysis for I-880 freeway study segments that are located to both north and
                  south of the Fremont Boulevard interchange. Under 2035 Baseline (No Project) Conditions, all the
                  freeway segments are expected to operate at LOS D or better during the peak hours. Under 2035 plus
                  Project Conditions, the directional volumes for all the segments are expected to increase by less than one
                  percent, so based on the established ACTC criteria for this study, this traffic volume increase is not
                  considered a significant impact.

                  TJKM additionally reviewed the project site plan with respect to site access, onsite traffic circulation, onsite
                  pedestrian circulation, vehicle parking, and bicycle parking facilities. Overall traffic circulation patterns
                  proposed throughout the site promote efficient circulation of autos.

                  In terms of bicycles, the applicant is planning to install bicycle racks. Additionally, it is recommended that
                  to be consistent with the City of Fremont Bicycle Master Plan guidelines and recommendations, the

                                                                                                                        Page 3
                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont              July 23, 2012
        TJKM
Transportation
   Consultants

                  project applicant consider providing lockers or secure bicycle storage within the building for employee
                  parking.

                  Analysis Methodology

                  Study Intersections and Scenarios
                  The City has identified the following study intersections for this traffic analysis study (associated traffic
                  controls are listed in parentheses):
                     1. Fremont Boulevard/Grimmer Boulevard (Signal)
                     2. Fremont Boulevard/I-880 NB Ramps (Signal)
                     3. Fremont Boulevard/I-880 SB Ramps (Signal)
                     4. Fremont Boulevard/Cushing Parkway (Signal)
                     5. Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway (One-way stop control)
                     6. Fremont Boulevard/W. Warren Avenue (Signal)
                     7. W. Warren Avenue/I-880 SB Ramps/Lakeview Boulevard (Signal)
                     8. W. Warren Avenue/I-880/NB Ramps (Signal)
                     9. Warren Avenue/Warm Springs Boulevard (Signal)
                     10. Mission Boulevard/Warm Springs Boulevard (Signal)

                  The peak periods of traffic data collection in the morning were between 7:00 a.m. and 9:00 a.m. and in
                  the afternoon between 4:00 p.m. and 6:00 p.m. Figure 1 shows the study intersections and proposed
                  project vicinity. Figure 2 shows the proposed Site Plan Alternative 1, and Figure 3 shows Alternative
                  2 of the proposed project site plans.

                  This study addresses the following three (3) traffic scenarios:
                      1. Existing Conditions ­ This scenario evaluates the study intersections based on existing traffic
                          counts and field surveys.
                      2. Background Conditions ­ This scenario is similar to Existing Conditions, but with the addition of
                          traffic from the approved and pending developments located in the City of Fremont. Traffic
                          generated by the currently being built - Pacific Commons retail land uses are also included.
                      3. Project Conditions ­ This scenario is similar to Background Conditions, but with the addition of
                          traffic from the proposed Delta Products Development.

                  Intersection Level of Service Analysis Methodology
                  Potential project traffic impacts on the study intersections were quantified through the determination
                  of level of service (LOS), a qualitative measure describing operational conditions within a traffic
                  stream. There are six levels of service defined for each type of facility (i.e., roadway or intersection)
                  that is analyzed. LOS has letter designations ranging from A to F, with LOS A representing free flow
                  traffic with little or no delay and LOS F representing jammed conditions with excessive delay and long
                  back-ups. Procedures for analyzing each type of facility are based on the Highway Capacity Manual
                  2000 (HCM 2000). The LOS methodology is described in detail in Appendix A.

                  Alameda County Transportation Commission Level of Service Analysis Methodology
                  Potential project traffic impacts on local Alameda County Congestion Management Program (CMP)
                  roadways were also evaluated using LOS measures of effectiveness identified in the most recent
                  (2009) Alameda County Transportation Commission (ACTC) LOS Monitoring Report, which relates
                  volume-to-capacity (v/c) ratios and travel speeds to LOS.




                                                                                                                        Page 5
                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont              July 23, 2012
        TJKM
Transportation
   Consultants

                  The ACTC analysis is required since the proposed project is expected to generate more than 100 net new
                  vehicle trips (ACTC threshold) during the weekday p.m. peak hour. The following CMP / Metropolitan
                  Transportation System (MTS) freeway facilities in the project vicinity were analyzed under Year 2035
                  Conditions both with and without proposed project traffic:
                      ·    I-880 North of Fremont Boulevard
                      ·    I-880 South of Fremont Boulevard

                  Significant Impact Criteria / Level of Service Standards
                  According to the City of Fremont's General Plan, the acceptable intersection level of service is LOS D.
                  A project would result in a significant adverse impact on traffic conditions at a signalized intersection
                  in the City of Fremont if for either peak hour:
                      ·    The level of service at the intersection degrades from an acceptable LOS D or better under
                           background conditions to an unacceptable LOS E or F under project conditions; or
                      ·    The level of service at the intersection is an unacceptable LOS under background conditions
                           and the addition of project trips causes the average delay at the intersection to increase by
                           four (4) or more seconds.

                  The Fremont General Plan does not specify LOS threshold criteria for unsignalized intersections.
                  According to the Alameda County Transportation Commission 2009 LOS Monitoring Report and
                  2007 Technical and Policy Guidelines, the LOS standard for CMP roadway network analysis is LOS E,
                  except where LOS F was the LOS of a segment when originally measured as part of the CMP, in which
                  case the standard shall be LOS F. However, the ACTC does not have a policy for determining a
                  threshold of significance for segments operating unacceptably without the project. Rather,
                  professional judgment is required to determine project level impacts. Therefore, for the purposes of
                  this traffic impact analysis, if a segment operates unacceptably without the project, the impacts of the
                  proposed project are considered significant if the contribution of project traffic is at least five percent
                  of the total traffic.

                  Existing Conditions

                  Roadway Network
                  Fremont Boulevard is a six-lane north-south arterial roadway that provides two access points to the project
                  south of Cushing Parkway. To the south this roadway connects Auto Mall Parkway and Grimmer
                  Boulevard with the I-880 interchange within the City of Fremont. The posted speed limit on this roadway in
                  the study area is 45 mph.

                  Cushing Parkway is a four-lane northwest-southeast arterial roadway that originates at the Fremont
                  Boulevard / I-880 interchange to the southeast and terminates at the intersection with Auto Mall Parkway
                  and Boyce Road. The posted speed limit on this roadway further west of the project site is
                  45 mph.

                  Mission Boulevard (Rte. 262) is a four-lane to six-lane roadway that runs east-west between the interstates, I-
                  880 and I-680. This is a vital interstate cross-connector roadway that facilitates regional access for bay area
                  commuters. The posted speed limit on this roadway is 45 mph.

                  Warm Springs Boulevard is a two-lane to six-lane north-south collector roadway that originates to the north
                  at Grimmer Boulevard and terminates to the south at Dixon Landing within the City of Fremont, providing
                  access along its route to various commercial and residential land uses. The posted speed limit on this
                  roadway is 45 mph.

                  Existing Transit Facilities
                  The proposed project is served by Alameda-Contra Costa Transit District (AC Transit) public bus service.
                  Two AC Transit routes (Routes 212 and 215) serves the project vicinity.

                  Route 212 operates within the
                  cities of Fremont and Newark,
                  providing service between the
                  New Park Mall and the Fremont
                  Bay Area Rapid Transit (BART)
                  Station at half-hour headways
                  between 6:00 a.m. and 9:30 p.m.
                  Stops serving the project site are
                  located on Cushing Parkway and
                  Fremont Boulevard.

                  Route 215 operates within the
                  City of Fremont between the
                  Landing Parkway/Fremont
                  Boulevard intersection and the
                  Fremont BART station. This bus
                  route operates at 45-minute
                  headways in both clockwise and
                  counterclockwise directions
                  between 6:45 a.m. and 3:00 p.m.
                  Currently there are no scheduled
                  bus-stops on Route 215 within
                  the walking distance of the
                  project site, but a future bus-stop is feasible.

                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont            July 23, 2012

                  Existing Bicycle and Pedestrian Facilities
                  TJKM assessed existing bicycle and pedestrian facility conditions through review of the 2012 City of
                  Fremont Bicycle Master Plan (exhibit below) and field surveys. Class II (on-street striped) bicycle lanes are
                  provided in the proposed project vicinity along Fremont Boulevard (south of W. Warren Avenue and
                  north of Industrial Place), Cushing Parkway, and Warm Springs Boulevard (south of W. Warren Avenue).
                  Fremont Boulevard adjacent to the project site is currently a Class III (shared roadway) bicycle route, but
                  the Bicycle Master Plan proposes Class II bicycle lanes on this segment in the future. The City is currently
                  conducting a Bay Trail Feasibility Study and working with San Francisco Bay Trails in determining potential
                  Bay Trail alignments through the area. One proposed Bay Trial Alignment being considered is located
                  immediately southwest of the project site and along the Alameda County Flood Control Channel Levee.
                  The study is estimated to be completed in December 2012. The project plan should consider trail access
                  connections to the Alameda County Flood Control Channel should it be designated as a Bay Trail or a
                  Connector Trail to the Bay Trail. In terms of pedestrian facilities, sidewalks are provided along area streets,
                  and crosswalks are provided at all study intersections at the existing project site.




                  Source: City of Fremont Bicycle Master Plan 2012

                  Existing Traffic Volumes
                  All Traffic Data (ATD) conducted peak hour turning movement counts during typical weekday a.m. and
                  p.m. peak periods (7:00 to 9:00 a.m. and 4:00 to 6:00 p.m., respectively) at the study intersections in
                  March 2012. Count sheets for the study intersections are included in Appendix B. Field verification of
                  existing intersection lane configurations and traffic controls were also conducted in March 2012 and
                  provided the basis for the level of service analysis for Existing Conditions.
                  Figure 4 illustrates the existing intersection turning movement volumes, lane geometry, and traffic
                  controls at the study intersections.
                                                                                                                      Page 11
                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont             July 23, 2012
        TJKM
Transportation
   Consultants


                  For the ACTC roadway analysis, TJKM consulted the latest published Alameda County Transportation
                  Demand Model volumes on its website. These model volumes were used as the basis for the ACTC
                  corridor analysis.

                  Intersection Level of Service Analysis ­ Existing Conditions
                  Table I below summarizes peak hour levels of service (LOS) at the study intersections under Existing
                  Conditions. LOS worksheets are provided in Appendix C. Under Existing Conditions, all the study
                  intersections are operating at an acceptable LOS C or better except for the intersection of Fremont
                  Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection during the p.m. peak hour. Currently, this is an unsignalized
                  intersection with stop control on the minor street which operates at LOS E with an average delay of
                  49.8 seconds/vehicle (sec/veh).

                  Signal Warrant Analysis ­ Existing Conditions
                  A signal warrant analysis was conducted for the study intersections under Existing Conditions. The
                  2006 California Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices (CA MUTCD) was used to determine
                  whether the unsignalized study intersection meets the criteria for installation of a traffic signal.
                  Installation should be considered if one or more of the warrant criteria described in the CA MUTCD
                  is met.

                  As part of this study, the peak hour warrant (Warrant 3) was analyzed for Fremont Boulevard/ Landing
                  Parkway, a one-way stop controlled intersection. The peak hour signal warrant is intended for locations
                  where for a minimum of one hour of an average day, the minor street traffic experiences undue delay
                  when entering and crossing the major street. Based on the peak hour traffic volume data, a peak hour
                  signal warrant is not met for the Existing Conditions during either the a.m. or the p.m. peak hours.

                                                                                                                                 Page 12
                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont                        July 23, 2012
        TJKM
Transportation
   Consultants

                  For example, during the a.m. peak hour the major street (Fremont Boulevard) volume is 1,425
                  vehicles/hour (veh/hr) and the minor approach volume is 131 veh/hr. However, the minor approach
                  volume threshold is 222 veh/hr for the afore-mentioned major street volume. Signal warrant analysis
                  information is provided along with LOS summary sheets under Appendix C.

                  TJKM also conducted collision analysis for this intersection and has found only one reported collision.
                  The collision was a rear-end type involving a southbound vehicle colliding with a stationary vehicle on
                  Fremont Boulevard during a weekday (7/27/2007) afternoon. Based on the number of collisions, CA
                  MUTCD based accident warrant is not met. A collision diagram for this intersection is provided at the
                  end of Appendix C.

                  Background Conditions (Existing plus Approved / Pending Projects)

                  This scenario is similar to Existing Conditions, but with the addition of traffic from the approved and
                  pending developments located within the City of Fremont. Traffic generated by currently built but
                  vacant existing Pacific Commons retail land uses are also included.

                  are expected to be built within the City of Fremont.

                  Intersection Level of Service Analysis ­ Background Conditions
                  Table III below summarizes peak hour levels of service (LOS) at the study intersections under

                  this is an unsignalized intersection with stop control on the minor street, which is expected to operate

                  Project Conditions (Background plus Proposed Project)

                  This scenario is similar to Background Conditions, but with the addition of traffic expected to be
                  generated by the proposed Delta Products Development.

                  The Project Conditions are analyzed under two scenarios: Alternative 1- southernmost project driveway
                  on Fremont Boulevard is offset from and located north of Landing Parkway intersection; and, Alternative
                  2 ­ Southernmost project driveway on Fremont Boulevard aligns with Landing Parkway centerline.

                  Project Proposal
                  The proposed Delta Products Development consists of a 178,327-sq. ft. of Research & Development
                  (R&D) three-story building. The currently vacant parcel of 15.5 acres is located at the southwest corner
                  of Fremont Boulevard/Cushing Parkway intersection.

                  Primary arterial access to the project site along Fremont Boulevard would be via a northerly right-
                  in/right-out (RI-RO) driveway and a southerly all-way access. An additional RI-RO driveway along
                  Cushing Parkway is located to the west of Fremont Boulevard. The southerly project access along
                  Fremont Boulevard is currently being analyzed with two alternatives (refer to Figure 2 and Figure 3).
                  It should be noted that the second alternative, which provides project access at the intersection of the
                  proposed driveway connection with Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway as shown on Figure 3, will
                  require the acquisition of an easement or right-of -way from the neighboring property owner to the
                  south.

                  Project Trip Generation
                  The Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) has compiled the results of trip generation research
                  from over 4,250 individual land use studies throughout the United States and Canada. The eight
                  edition of Trip Generation contains trip generation rates for over 140 different land use codes. Trip
                  generation rates for the proposed project are based on data published in this manual. Table IV shows
                  the expected trip generation for the proposed project based on ITE trip generation rates, as well as
                  expected trip discounts for the project site.

                  As shown in the table below, the proposed Delta Products R&D Development (ITE Land Use Code ­
                  760) is expected to generate a total of 1,446 daily trips, including 218 a.m. peak hour trips and
                  191 p.m. peak hour trips on a typical weekday.

                  Table IV: Proposed Project Trip Generation - Weekday
                                                                 Daily    Weekday A.M. Peak Hour   Weekday P.M. Peak Hour

                  Project Trip Distribution and Assignment
                  Trip distribution assumptions for the proposed project were developed based on existing travel
                  patterns, knowledge of the study area, and our experience with the other traffic studies within the City
                  of Fremont.

                  The trip distribution assumptions are listed below:
                      ·    30 percent to/from the north via Fremont Boulevard
                      ·    20 percent to/from the north via I-880
                      ·    12 percent to/from the south via I-880
                      ·    10 percent to/from the west via Cushing Parkway
                      ·    12 percent to/from Warm Springs area via Warren Avenue
                      ·    3 percent to/ from the south via Fremont Boulevard
                      ·    3 percent to/from the north of I-680 via Mission Boulevard
                      ·    5 percent to/from the south of I-680 via Mission Boulevard
                      ·    5 percent to/from the east via Mission Boulevard

                  The trip distribution assumptions at the study intersections for the proposed project are illustrated in
                  Figure 6. The resulting trip assignment assumptions at the study intersections for the two alternatives of
                  the proposed site plan are shown in Figures 7 and 8, respectively.

                  The assigned trips were added to Background Conditions traffic volumes to generate Project
                  Conditions traffic volumes. The resulting intersection turning movement volumes at the study
                  intersections for Project Conditions based on the two alternative site plans are shown in Figure 9 and
                  Figure 10, respectively.

                  Intersection Level of Service Analysis ­ Project Conditions
                  Table V summarizes the results of the intersection LOS and delay analysis under Project Conditions.
                  Detailed LOS calculations are included in Appendix E. Under Project Conditions, all the study
                  intersections are operating at an acceptable LOS D or better except for Fremont Boulevard/Landing
                  Parkway intersection. During the p.m. peak hour, this unsignalized study intersection is expected to
                  operate at LOS F with a minor street average delay of 50.7 sec/veh for Alternative 1. Under
                  Alternative 2, the Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway/project access intersection would operate at
                  LOS F in both the a.m. peak hour and the p.m. peak hour with two-way stop control on the minor
                  streets. The project driveway (minor street) approach delay for Alternative 2 is over 120sec/veh.

                  It is recommended that the project access be provided at the existing T-intersection of Fremont
                  Boulevard/Landing Parkway (i.e., Alternative 2 site plan), and that the intersection be signalized and an
                  exclusive left-turn lane be added on the northbound approach to provide acceptable LOS operations.

                  Signal Warrant Analysis ­ Project Conditions
                  A signal warrant analysis was conducted for the intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway
                  under Project Conditions. Based on the peak hour traffic volume data, a peak hour signal warrant is
                  not met for the Project Conditions during both the peak hours; however, the installation of a traffic
                  signal is recommended at this intersection. The site access, parking and circulation section includes
                  further discussion on this signal. Signal warrant analysis information is provided along with LOS
                  summary sheets under Appendix E.

                  Site Access, Parking and Circulation

                  TJKM reviewed two alternative site plans provided by Kier & Wright Civil Engineers (K&W) dated
                  2/27/2012, with respect to: driveway locations and operational characteristics; on-site vehicle
                  circulation, including truck access; parking layout; and pedestrian circulation. The two site plan
                  alternatives reviewed are referenced as follows:
                       1. Full-access shared entry at Fremont Boulevard/ Landing Parkway (Alt. 2- Figure 3)
                       2. Right-turn-only access on Fremont Boulevard north of Landing Parkway (Alt. 1- Figure 2)

                  I.       Full-Access Shared Entry at Landing Parkway
                  As shown in Figure 3, this alternative would provide three access driveway connections to adjacent
                  public streets as follows:
                      · A full-access driveway that would create a new west leg at the existing Fremont
                           Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection
                      · A right-turn in/right-turn out driveway on Fremont Boulevard approximately midway between
                           Cushing Parkway and Landing Parkway
                      · A right-turn-in/right-turn-out driveway on Cushing Parkway at the northwest corner of the
                           site, approximately 400 feet west of the limit line at the intersection with Fremont Boulevard

                  Driveways - The full-access driveway location at the Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection
                  would provide the best directional access for traffic entering and exiting the site. A driveway at this
                  intersection would provide better driveway spacing with no sight-distance issues. Based on the
                  preliminary site plan, the driveway would provide three exit lanes approaching Fremont Boulevard,
                  consisting of two left-turn lanes and one shared through-right lane. TJKM recommends revising this
                  exit lane configuration to provide one left-turn, one through, and one right-turn lane, a detail that can
                  be addressed in the design phase of the project. A raised median would separate the exit lanes from a
                  single entry lane 20 feet wide, which would provide adequate capacity for traffic entering the site from
                  Fremont Boulevard or Landing Parkway. The 20-foot entry lane width, along with the 40-foot corner
                  curb radius shown on the plan, would not provide adequate room for trucks turning right from
                  southbound Fremont Boulevard unless they start their turn from the second traffic lane away from the
                  curb. TJKM recommends a 60-foot corner curb radius and a 24-foot width for the first 50 feet of the
                  entry lane to allow trucks to turn right from the curb lane on Fremont Boulevard. The exit lane
                  widths, along with the 40-foot curb radius on the southwest corner shown on the plan, would provide
                  adequate room for exiting trucks turning onto Fremont Boulevard.

                  The installation of a traffic signal and the addition of an exclusive left-turn lane on the northbound
                  approach are recommended at the proposed full-access driveway at the intersection of Fremont
                  Boulevard/Landing Parkway. A traffic signal at this intersection would improve operations from LOS F
                  to LOS B (as shown on Table V), and improves vehicle circulation to and from the project site. The
                  traffic volumes and vehicle speeds along Fremont Boulevard, which has a posted speed limit of 45 mph,
                  may make it difficult for motorists to make left turns out of the project's driveway without a traffic
                  signal.

                  The site plan (as shown in Figure 3) indicates a possible future parking lot on the adjacent parcel to the
                  south, and shows it connecting to the project's full-access driveway exit lanes at the beginning of the
                  corner curb radius at Fremont Boulevard, which would be a very poor location for safe and effective
                  operations. TJKM recommends that any connection to the full-access driveway should be located at


                                                                                                                     Page 27
                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont            July 23, 2012
        TJKM
Transportation
   Consultants

                  least 150 feet from the intersection with Fremont Boulevard. No other throat distance issues are
                  identified for this driveway.

                  The other driveway location on Fremont Boulevard would be located approximately 375 feet south of
                  Cushing Parkway and 450 feet north of Landing Parkway, which would provide good spacing from
                  adjacent intersections and driveways relative to right turns in and out of the driveway. However, the
                  proximity of this driveway to the Cushing Parkway intersection combined with the roadway curvature
                  and prevailing speeds on Fremont Boulevard, plus conflicts with existing left turn access to commercial
                  driveways on the east side of Fremont Boulevard, would present significant issues for potential left-turn
                  access at this driveway location. TJKM recommends that this driveway be restricted to right-turn-
                  in/right-turn-out access only, for which the proposed location provides adequate sight-distance. The
                  site plan shows a 35-foot wide, two-lane driveway that would suffice for a right-turn-only access at
                  Fremont Boulevard. The distance between Fremont Boulevard and the closest intersecting internal
                  driveway aisle is adequate at the approximately 150 feet shown.

                  The City of Fremont has indicated that Caltrans, which controls the intersection of Cushing Parkway
                  and Fremont Boulevard, may be installing an eastbound right turn arrow at this intersection, which
                  would necessitate the prohibition of U-turns on northbound to southbound Fremont Boulevard at the
                  intersection. This action would preclude traffic coming from the south on Fremont Boulevard desiring
                  to use this northern driveway via the standard U-turn movement. The northern driveway on Fremont
                  Boulevard seems to be the "ceremonial" entrance to the building with a landscaped water feature near
                  the entrance, and is likely to be designated for visitors and other non-employees. However, this
                  driveway would still be functional for traffic coming from the west and north on Cushing Parkway and
                  from the Fremont Boulevard/I-880 interchange, which provides good access from both travel directions
                  on I-880.

                  The third driveway is located on Cushing Parkway near the west property line of the parcel. It is
                  approximately 400 feet in advance of the intersection of Cushing Parkway and Fremont Boulevard.
                  Cushing Parkway has a median at this location, which would allow only right in/right out movements at
                  the driveway. It is not desirable to construct a median break at this intersection because of its
                  proximity to the signalized intersection and the inability to provide a left turn storage lane. However,
                  there is an existing median break even closer to Fremont Boulevard, located about 150 feet west of the
                  proposed driveway. The concern related to this median break (which is equipped with an east bound
                  left turn lane) is that motorists exiting from the proposed Delta driveway who would desire to travel
                  westbound on Cushing Parkway would need to cut across three traffic lanes, enter the left turn lane,
                  and make a U-turn at the median break. With only 150 feet to make such a maneuver, this could be
                  potentially hazardous. One solution would be to prohibit eastbound to westbound U-turns at the
                  median break in the future, if the movement described develops into an actual problem.

                  On-site vehicle and truck circulation - The on-site circulation is satisfactory. There are two main parking
                  lots, on the northwest corner of the site (northern parking lot) and on the southwest corner of the site
                  (southern parking lot). These are primarily intended to serve employees and are situated convenient to
                  employee entrances to the building. Both parking lots can be reached from each of the three driveways,
                  although the northern parking lot is primarily accessible to traffic coming from the west on Cushing
                  Parkway or from the north using the northern Fremont Boulevard driveway.

                  The southern parking lots are convenient to all traffic using Fremont Boulevard. The truck docks for
                  the site are located on the southern edge of the building complex and are conveniently reached only
                  from the southern driveway on Fremont Boulevard. Trucks are not required to drive through any of
                  the vehicular parking lots or aisles, so the truck access features are very good. There is a large
                                                                                                                     Page 28
                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont            July 23, 2012
        TJKM
Transportation
   Consultants

                  rectangular area near the truck docks (approximately 157 feet by 120 feet) that will allow trucks to
                  turn around and to back into the six loading docks.

                  Parking layout - This plan appears to satisfy the requirement of Article 20 of the Fremont Zoning
                  Ordinance as to the number of parking stalls as well as the required dimensions of the parking stalls
                  themselves. The layout of the parking lots provides for very convenient access to all parking stalls.
                  There are a number of parking stalls that are compact in size, as allowed by the zoning ordinance.
                  These stalls, which tend to be the least desirable from a user standpoint, are located in the most distant
                  portions of the parking lots, which is a good idea. One exception to this approach is the visitor parking
                  area near the main entrance to the building. There are about 18 stalls in this area which appear to be all
                  compact size. The dimensions of this area should be adjusted to accommodate full size vehicles.

                  Pedestrian and bicycle circulation/access - The site plan shows six-foot wide sidewalks along the entire
                  frontage of Cushing Parkway and Fremont Boulevard . In addition, at three locations, sidewalks connect
                  with the building from the streets. The site plans show bicycle racks located in three separate areas, all
                  convenient to employee entrances to the buildings. Bicycle lanes are planned for both streets fronting
                  the site, and the frontage improvements for this project would allow for these lanes to be installed.

                  Fremont Boulevard Frontage - The frontage improvement requirements for this project will allow
                  Fremont Boulevard to be "completed" to its ultimate standards. At the northern portion of the site
                  near Cushing Parkway, Fremont Boulevard widens to accommodate three southbound lanes, and
                  a total of seven northbound lanes ­ two for left turns, four for through traffic, and one for right turns.
                  Further south, the roadway will narrow to two lanes in each direction, plus a center turn lane. (There
                  will also be bicycle lanes in each direction with a minimum width of five feet.) This report recommends
                  signalizing the Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection, which will need to have exclusive left
                  turn lanes on both Fremont Boulevard approaches, northbound and southbound. The area north of
                  the new traffic signal also has three existing driveways on the east side of Fremont Boulevard, providing
                  access to three hotels and a service station. The northern of these three driveways is already blocked
                  by a median forcing right in/right out movements only, while the other two have unlimited access.
                  TJKM recommends that the two southern driveways on the east side of Fremont Boulevard continue
                  to have access via a center two-way left turn lane.

                  2.      Right-Turn-Only Access North of Landing Parkway
                  As shown in Figure 2, this is an alternative site plan proposed by the applicant. The site plan shown on
                  Figure 2 is on land entirely under control of the applicant; the plan addressed above requires the use of a
                  portion of the parcel immediately to the south in order to allow for the southern driveway to be aligned
                  with Landing Parkway. In this discussion, only the differences between the two plans will be discussed.

                  The essential difference between the two plans is the location of the southern driveway on Fremont
                  Boulevard. In Figure 2, the project access is located about 200 feet north of Landing Parkway, or about
                  midway between the northern driveway and the Landing Parkway intersection. A driveway at this
                  location presents several disadvantages when compared with the other plan:
                      1. A driveway at this location interferes with the existing southbound left-turn lane for Landing
                          Parkway, because a significant number of vehicles exiting the driveway are likely to cut
                          straight across the southbound through lanes to enter the left-turn lane, and then attempt an
                          awkward U-turn to proceed northbound on Fremont Boulevard.
                      2. This location would not accommodate a northbound left turn into the site because of the
                          proximity of Landing Parkway.


                                                                                                                     Page 29
                 Final Report ­ Traffic Study for Delta Products Development in the City of Fremont            July 23, 2012
        TJKM
Transportation
   Consultants

                      3. In this plan (as well as the plan described above) all truck access is contemplated to use the
                         southern driveway. This location is not a candidate for signalization, which would make
                         truck access into and out of the south very awkward, particularly for trucks arriving from the
                         south.

                  It is possible that a driveway at this location could be considered temporary with the idea that it would
                  be relocated to align with Landing Parkway when the parcel to the south is developed. However, if the
                  development to the south is delayed, use of a driveway at this location would be considered
                  unacceptable. In fact, a superior temporary location might be the actual southern limits of the parcel
                  being developed. While this would still misalign the driveway with Landing Parkway, the misalignment of
                  about 75 feet might be superior to the 200 feet shown on Figure 2 because it would allow the
                  intersection of Fremont Boulevard and Landing Parkway to operate more normally. However, it is clear
                  that this location is not acceptable as a long-term solution for the southern driveway. Per City of
                  Fremont Development Policy, an access driveway cannot be located within 100 feet of an intersection.
                  Under the Project Alternative 1, the site plan shows that the project driveway is located approximately
                  180 feet to the north of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection and thus the distance criterion
                  for project driveway does not conflict with the City's policy. All other aspects of the evaluation of the
                  site plan shown on Figure 2 are identical to the description above related to the site plan shown on
                  Figure 3.

                  Queuing Analysis
                  TJKM conducted a queuing and vehicle storage analysis at all study intersections for Existing,
                  Background, and Project Conditions based on weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hour volumes developed
                  for each scenario. TJKM analyzed 95th percentile (maximum) queues using the HCM 2000 Queue
                  methodology contained in Traffix software for all left and right turn pockets at the ten study
                  intersections for each scenario under weekday a.m. and p.m. peak hours.

                  It should be noted that the eastbound right turn lane at Fremont Boulevard/Cushing Parkway has a
                  95th percentile queue length of 425 feet during the a.m. peak hour of Existing conditions. With the
                  plus project conditions, the right turn queue length would almost extend to the right-in/right-out
                  driveway (425 feet from stop line) on Cushing Parkway. TJKM qualitatively analyzed this intersection
                  with an eastbound right-turn overlap with northbound left-turn lane and finds that there is no
                  improvement in the queue conditions for the EBRT lane. The queue lengths are available on the LOS
                  summary sheets for all the scenarios under appendices.

                  Project Driveways
                  TJKM similarly analyzed expected Project Conditions volumes at the project driveways using the
                  HCM 2000 Queue methodology contained in Traffix in terms of expected 95th percentile queue
                  lengths. As shown in Table VII, queue lengths for all turns into the project site are expected to be
                  normal (three vehicle length of 75 feet or below) and should be well-contained within the storage
                  bays to be provided. As shown in the table, the northbound left-turn has a 95th percentile queue
                  length of two vehicles under Project Alternative 2. Though two vehicles would just require a storage
                  length of 50 feet, to accommodate an occasional truck in the northbound left-turn lane, a storage
                  length of 75 feet is recommended.

                  The deceleration length for an auxiliary traffic lane with a posted speed limit of 45 mph is 340 feet,
                  based on the guidance provided by American Association of Highway State Highway and Transportation
                  Officials (AASHTO) publication of Geometric Design of Highways and Streets. However, on many
                  roadway facilities, it is not practical to provide full length of auxiliary lane for deceleration since on
                                                                                                                       Page 30

        TJKM

                  some occasions storage length overrides the deceleration length. Based on the project trips and
                  local geometry, TJKM does not recommend any acceleration lanes.

                  ACTC Informational Analysis

                  As required by the 2009 Alameda County Congestion Management Program (CMP), I-880 both north
                  and south of the Fremont Boulevard interchange were evaluated under Year 2035 Conditions both
                  without and with the proposed project. The purpose was to determine the potential impacts, if any,
                  with respect to proposed project traffic on ACTC facilities in the immediate vicinity, since the
                  proposed project is expected to generate more than 100 p.m. peak hour trips.

                  Freeway a.m. and p.m. peak hour volumes for years 2035 were based on the travel demand model
                  volumes published on Alameda County Transportation Commission website:
                  http://www.alamedactc.org. The year 2035 plus Project volumes were developed by adding project
                  trips to the 2035 baseline volumes.

                  According to the ACTC 2009 LOS Monitoring Report and 2007 Technical and Policy Guidelines, the
                  LOS standard for ACTC analysis is LOS E, except where LOS F was the LOS of a segment when
                  originally measured as part of the CMP, in which case the standard shall be
                  LOS F. However, the ACTC does not have a policy for determining a threshold of significance for
                  segments operating unacceptably without the project. Rather, professional judgment is required to
                  determine project level impacts. Therefore, for the purposes of this traffic impact analysis, if a
                  segment operates unacceptably without the project, the impacts of the proposed project are
                  considered significant if the contribution of project traffic is at least five percent of the total traffic.

                  2035 Baseline vs. plus Project Analysis
                  Table VIII shows the results of a LOS analysis for the 2035 analysis scenarios both with and without
                  the proposed project. Under 2035 Baseline (No Project) Conditions, majority of the study segments
                  are expected to operate unacceptably as shown in Table VII. Under 2035 plus Project Conditions, all
                  study segment's volume-to-capacity ratio is expected to increase by less than one percent. Based on
                  the established ACTC criteria for this study, this amount of percent increase is not considered a
                  significant impact.

                  With the addition of proposed project traffic to 2035 Baseline Conditions, the freeway segment LOS
                  and its corresponding V/C does not change considerably as shown in the table below. Therefore, no
                  significant impacts were found with the addition of proposed project trips to the freeway peak hour
                  volumes.

                  Conclusions

                  TJKM has reached the following conclusions regarding the proposed Delta Products Development in
                  the City of Fremont:
                      · The proposed Delta Products Development of 178,327 sq. ft. is expected to generate a total
                          of 1,446 daily trips, including 218 a.m. peak hour trips and 191 p.m. peak hour trips on a
                          typical weekday.
                      ·    Under Existing Conditions, all the study intersections are operating at an acceptable LOS D or
                           better except for the intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection during
                           the p.m. peak hour.
                      ·    Under Background Conditions with the addition of approved / pending project traffic, all the
                           study intersections are expected to continue to operate at an acceptable LOS D or better
                           except for the intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection during the
                           p.m. peak hour.
                      ·    Under Project Conditions, with the addition of project traffic to the Background Conditions,
                           all the study intersections are expected to continue to operate at an acceptable LOS D or
                           better except for the intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway intersection.
                           During the p.m. peak hour, this unsignalized study intersection is expected to operate at
                           LOS F with a minor street average delay of 50.7 sec/veh for Alternative 1. Under
                           Alternative 2, the Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway/project access intersection would
                           operate at LOS F in both the a.m. peak hour and the p.m. peak hour with two-way stop
                           control on the minor streets. It is recommended that the project access be provided at
                           the existing T-intersection of Fremont Boulevard/Landing Parkway, and that the
                           intersection be signalized and an exclusive left-turn lane be added on the northbound
                           approach to provide acceptable LOS operations.
                      ·    TJKM conducted Alameda County CMP analysis for I-880 freeway study segments that are
                           located to both north and south of the Fremont Boulevard interchange. Under 2035 Baseline
                           (No Project) Conditions, majority of the study segments are expected to operate
                           unacceptably. Under 2035 plus Project Conditions, all study segment's volume-to-capacity
                           ratio is expected to increase by less than one percent. Based on the established ACTC criteria
                           for this study, less than one percent increase is not considered a significant impact.
                      ·    TJKM additionally reviewed the project site plan with respect to site access, onsite traffic
                           circulation, onsite pedestrian circulation, vehicle parking, and bicycle parking facilities.
                           Overall traffic circulation patterns proposed throughout the site promote efficient circulation
                           of autos.
                      ·    In terms of bicycles, it is recommended that to be consistent with the City of Fremont
                           Bicycle Master Plan guidelines and recommendations, the project applicant consider
                           providing lockers for use by site employees.

                 Appendix A ­ Level of Service Methodology
      DESCRIPTION OF SIGNALIZED INTERSECTION CAPACITY ANALYSIS
                        Updated 2000 HCM METHOD


Background

The operations method of intersection capacity analysis found in Chapter 16, "Signalized
Intersections," of the Highway Capacity Manual 2000, Transportation Research Board, was used
for this study. This method is used in most analyses of existing conditions or of future situations
in which traffic, geometric, and control parameters were well established by projections and trial
designs.

This method addresses the capacity and level of service of intersection approaches, and the level
of service of the intersection as a whole. In this method, capacity and level of service are
evaluated separately, and are not related to each other in a simple one-to-one fashion. Capacity is
evaluated in terms of the ratio of demand flow rate to capacity (volume-to-capacity ratio), while
level of service is evaluated on the basis of control delay per vehicle (sec/veh).

The capacity of the intersection as a whole is not addressed by this method; the design and
signalization of intersections focuses on the accommodation of the major movements and
approaches comprising the intersection. Capacity is, therefore, only meaningful as applied to
these major movements and approaches. Capacity analysis results in the computation of volume-
to-capacity ratios for individual movements and a composite volume-to-capacity ratio for the sum
of critical movements or lane groups within the intersection. The volume-to-capacity ratio is the
actual or projected rate of flow on an approach or designated group of lanes during a peak 15-
minute interval divided by the capacity of the approach or designated group of lanes.

Level of Service

Level of service is based on the control delay per vehicle for various movements within the
intersection. While volume-to-capacity affects delay, there are other parameters that more
strongly affect it, such as the quality of progression, length of green phases, cycle lengths, and
others. Thus for any given volume-to-capacity ratio, a range of delay values my result, and vice-
versa. See the table "Level of Service Criteria for Signalized Intersections" for the relationship
between the level of service and stopped delay per vehicle.

Because delay is a complex measure, its relationship to capacity is also complex. It is possible,
for example, to have delays in the range of Level of Service F while the volume-to-capacity ratios
is below 1.00, perhaps as slow as 0.75-0.85. Very high delays can occur at such volume-to-
capacity ratios when some combination of the following conditions exists: the cycle length is
long; the lane group in question has a long red time; and/or the signal progression for the subject
movement is poor.

The reverse is also possible. A saturated approach or lane group with a volume-to-capacity equal
to 1.00 may have low delays if the cycle length is short, and/or the signal progression is favorable
for the subject movement. Acceptable delay levels do not automatically ensure that capacity is
sufficient. The analysis must consider the results of the capacity analysis module and the level of
service module to obtain a complete picture of existing or projected intersection operations.




                                                      c:\tjkm\templates\appendices-pleasanton office\sign. method 2000.doc
                                                                                                                  07/17/02
Thus, the designation of Level of Service does not automatically imply that the intersection,
approach, or lane group is overloaded, nor does a level of service in the A to E range
automatically imply that there is unused capacity available.

The procedures of this methodology require the analysis of both capacity and level of service
conditions to fully evaluate the operation of a signalized intersection.

Input Data

The input data necessary to use this methodology are:

·    Lane geometrics
·    Traffic volumes
·    Signal timing
·    Vehicle type distribution
·    Percent grade
·    Pedestrians
·    Peak hour factors
·    Parking activity
·    Arrival type per approach



Reference: Highway Capacity Manual, Special Report No. 209, Transportation Research Board, 2000.

               DESCRIPTION OF INTERSECTION CAPACITY ANALYSIS
                         UNSIGNALIZED 2000 METHOD


Background

The method of unsignalized intersection capacity analysis used in this study is from Chapter 17,
"Unsignalized Intersections" of the Highway Capacity Manual, Special report No. 209,
Transportation Research Board, updated October 2000.

This method applies to two-way STOP sign or YIELD sign controlled intersections (or one-way
STOP sign or YIELD sign controlled intersections at three-way intersections). At such
intersections, drivers on the minor street are forced to use judgement when selecting gaps in the
major flow through which to execute crossings or turning maneuvers. Thus, the capacity of the
controlled legs of an intersection is based on three factors:

1. The distribution of gaps in the major street traffic stream.
2. Driver judgement in selecting gaps through which to execute their desired maneuvers.
3. Follow-up time required to move into the front-of-queue position.

It is assumed that gaps in the traffic stream are randomly distributed. For this reason, the
methodology will be less reliable in situations in which the conflicting flows are strongly
platooned, as would be the case at many urban intersections where the major street is part of a
signalized network.

This method assumes that major street traffic is not affected by minor street flows. This
assumption is generally good for periods when the operation is smooth and uncongested. (When
congestion occurs, it is likely that major street traffic will experience some impedance due to
minor street traffic.) Left turns from the major street are assumed to be affected by the opposing
major street flow, and minor street traffic is affected by all conflicting movements.

Input Data

The general procedure to calculate the level of service is as follows:

1. Define existing geometric and volume conditions for the intersection under study.
2. Determine the conflicting traffic through which each minor street movement and the major
   street left-turn must cross.
3. Determine the size of the gap in the conflicting traffic stream needed by vehicles in each
   movement crossing the conflicting traffic stream.
4. Determine the capacity of the gaps in the major traffic stream to accommodate each of the
   subject movements that will utilize these gaps.
5. Adjust the capacities found to account for impedance and the use of shared lanes.
6. Estimate the average total delay for each of the subject movements and determine the level of
   service for each movement and for the intersection.


Gaps are utilized by vehicles in the following priority order:


                                                      c:\tjkm\templates\appendices-pleasanton office\unsig. method 2000.doc
                                                                                                                 07/17/2002
1.   Right turns from the minor street
2.   Left turns from the major street
3.   Through movements from the minor street
4.   Left turns from the minor street

For example, if a left-turning vehicle on the major street and a through vehicle from the minor
street are waiting to cross the major traffic stream, the first available gap of acceptable size would
be taken by the left-turning vehicle. The minor street through vehicle must wait for the second
available gap. In aggregate terms, a large number of such left-turning vehicles could use up so
many of the available gaps that minor street through vehicles are severely impeded or unable to
make safe crossing movements.

Level of Service

See the following table "Level of Service Criteria for Unsignalized Intersections" for the
relationship between delay and level of service.

                                    LEVEL OF SERVICE CRITERIA
                                 FOR UNSIGNALIZED ITNERSECTIONS

      Control Delay (s/veh)                         Level of Service                                       Delays
                 0-10                                        A                                     Little or no delay
           > 10-15 s/veh                                     B                                    Short traffic delays
           > 15-25 s/veh                                     C                                 Average traffic delays
           > 25-35 s/veh                                     D                                    Long traffic delays
            >35-50 s/veh                                     E                                Very long traffic delays
              > 50 s/veh                                      F                                 Extreme traffic delay


The level of service criteria for Two-Way STOP controlled intersections is somewhat different
from the criteria used in Chapter 16 for signalized intersections. The primary reason for this is
the difference that drivers expect a signalized intersection to carry higher traffic volumes than
unsignalized intersections. Additionally, several driver behavior conditions combine to make
delays at signalized intersections less onerous than at unsignalized intersections.

Reference: Highway Capacity Manual, Special Report 209, Transportation Research Board, Update October 2000.
